0 AUCTION BID~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
Syntax: Bid or Bid <amount of coins>
Syntax: Auction <item> <minimum coin bid> <y/n> or Auction halt

If I wanted to sell my steel dagger, I would type: Auction dagger 400 n
This would set the auction for my dagger at 400 copper coins (4 gold)
without autotransfer (type auction alone for more info on autoxfer.)
If nobody buys the item in an allotted time, it will close the
auction, freeing the channel for other auctioners.

If "Going twice" has not yet been heard, you can remove the item from the
auction block by typing Auction halt.  Abusing this to frustrate players
will start mean mobs hunting you, and/or you will become and outlaw.

Bid, with nothing after is shows you the item currently for sale and the
current bid, or the minimum if no-one has bid.
Bid <amount> sets your bid on the item currently for auction.  Note: you
may not bid more than the total coins you have in the bank and on your
person.  Note: if you spam the mud with bids of 1 increment, it is likely
that certain mobs will start hunting you, and you may become an outlaw!

See Also: BID, SOLD
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
~

0 SOLD~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
Once an item is sold by auction, you must contact the other player and
arrange a time/place to meet and exchange the object and money.  The best
place to do this is in the auction house or bank if the buying party
needs to withdraw cash.  You may want to arrange friends to be present
just in case the other party decides to take off with your cash or the
object!  Note: YES, this is legal, don't come crying to gods about it.
There is a chance if you rip someone off that mobs will start hunting you
and/or you will become an outlaw.  You have been warned :)

See Also: AUCTION, BID
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
~

0 POLICY POLICIES~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
Ignore the following.  There is no policy on whining since I will never
be online to see people whine.

This policy is simple for some, but may also get some deleted.

If you rag on the mud or a god in any way, shape or form, your character will
be frozen for two days minimum.  This includes calling gods cheaters (which
we aren't), complaining that something is totally unfair (see bottom note),
or calling the mud lame.  To get him/her unfrozen, you must write a
serious letter of appology to kilith@gryphonmud.com (I don't mean letters
like, "I think I was justified because" -- this'll just get you frozen
longer). If you can convince me that you will no longer insult the mud or
the god you insulted in the letter, you will be unfrozen after two days.
If not, tough luck... go play another mud or start a newbie.

Anyone starting a newbie after having their character frozen to whine or
TALK (ie argue) will get both their normal character deleted, and that
site newbie-banned.  If you feel you have something to discuss, write.

As always, it's my discretion whether or not you're ragging on the mud or
not, and all I have to say is, if you rag on the mud or any god just a bit,
you better hope I'm in a damn good mood, or you can take a two day siesta
from the mud.

If you are upset and feel you can't stop from complaining, calling the
situation unfair, calling a god a cheater, etc..., I strongly recommend
logging off before you open your mouth and get your character frozen.

Please NOTE: If you feel a situation really needs looking at (ie, a player is
abusing something, multiplaying, or there is a bug and you are stuck some-
where, etc), then feel free to send a pray.  As long as your attitude isn't
one of some uncontrolled teenager's frantic whining, I'll probably investigate
and do whatever it takes to get the situation fixed.

General rule: Think before you open your mouth, and take a break or complain
to other players if you are pissed.  If you ask us, "Why'd you do that?"
I'll probably answer.  If you respond "but blah blah.. whine whine, complain"
I'll probably justify my standpoint slightly.  If you continue to disagree
and spam my screen (I am often doing room descripts), you'll be frozen.
Simple.  Most of you will never have any problems with this :)
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
~

0 RULES RULE~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
On Void of Reality, we try to keep rules to a minimum.  Most of the rules
are hard-coded in, and cannot be broken due to software prevention.
However, you should be aware of certain rules to avoid character deletion:

0. READ AND UNDERSTAND HELP POLICY.

1. RULE:  Multiplaying is LIMITED!!

NOTE: An easy way to get your characters deleted and site-banned is to
      log in a good character, then log in an evil character for a second
      to check who is currently playing on the evil side or spy.  This is
      a serious offense, and will result in deletion the very first time
      you are caught breaking this multi-play rule.

      Also another way of being deleted is by using a second character
      as a storage character. I do check logs and if I find your second
      character logging on and off while your first character is online
      your second character will be deleted with out notice or warning.
      If I also find short logins on your characters I will check into it
      and if one is loaded with EQ it will be deleted.

FAQ: What happens if someone is playing from my same site, but we are
     not multiplaying and I get accused?
ANS: You will be investigated.  Both characters' email addresses will be
     mailed, and you will notice it writes to the logs when you connect
     from the same site of someone who is already playing.  Most of all,
     don't worry; if you provided and accurate email address everything will
     be cleared and you may continue playing as usual.
FAQ: How do you check for storage characters?
ANS: Every two days we run a program that notifies us of low level characters
     that have quite a few items.  We investigate from there by email address
     to determine if it is indeed a storage character.


2. RULE: No scripting.  Using a client or script language to play your
   character for you is illegal.  If your character is found to be repeating
   a loop of easy kills, you will be investigated.
   CONSEQUENCE: Instant deletion of your character.
   EXCEPTIONS: Casting spells to get better is fine I have no problem  
   but if you are caught BOTING for xp you WILL be DELETED!!
FAQ: What if I like hanging out in a low-level area?
ANS: 'Tis fine, just don't let us catch you repeating a command-loop.

FAQ: Is it ok to stay in newbies after level 40?
ANS: No and if you are caught all levels over 40 will be lost.
{R}*So that noone thinks you can stay in newbies if you are not scripting*{N}

3. RULE: No spamming.
   CONSEQUENCE:  If you are caught spamming players or channels, (this
   INCLUDES the auction and pray channels!) you will be deleted and your
   site will either be newbie-banned or permanently banned.  If you aren't a
   total dick, you can probably apologize in email and I can lift the ban in
   a few days.

4. RULE: All bugs must be reported.
   CONSEQUENCE:  If I watch you exploit a bug that is used to crash the
   mud or cheat, and you do not report it, you risk being deleted and
   sitebanned.  This is the rule I am most strict about, sorry folx :P


That's all for the rules.. remember, might makes right, and get some
friends so that berserk backstabbing dork doesn't getcha while you sleep!
We don't encourage player killing between good/good evil/evil, but it CAN
happen occasionally!  Kills sometimes get stolen too... tough shit!

See Also: MULTI, PKILLING
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
~

0 CHALLENGE~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
If, for some reason, you wish to fight a player but not to the death, you
can now do it in the arena.  Both players must be at full hit points, and
the format is challenge <player>.  The challenged player must then type
accept or decline, or he may turn challenge off.  After the waiting room
and battle, you will be transported with full hit points back to where
you were.  To cancel a challenge, type challenge <player> cancel.

You may turn Challenges OFF... See help CONFIG.
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
~

0 IGNORE~
Format: Ignore <annoying person name here>

Ignore with no argument will show you who you are currently ignoring.
You may ignore up to 10 people, and when ignored, no says, gossips,
tells, replies, or anything will be seen from them.  This can be a life
saver with poor-sport newbies who get on to annoy you because you killed
their character :)  ALWAYS report spamming characters through a note,
telling at what time they spammed you, and exactly what happened.  Often
spammers will be immediately sitebanned.

~

That's all folx!  Happy mudding... and remember.. it's just a game :P

Disapproving gods may take action by sending a mob to hunt you down or

between whitie/darkie is reason for deletion too.

0 GROUPING 'GROUPING COMMANDS'~
Follow: See HELP FOLLOW.
Group : See HELP GROUP.

Gtell : Syntax Gtell <text>.  This command tells <text> to your group.
Split : Syntax Split <amount>.  This command splits up money evenly.  Valid
        examples are: split 7 gold, split 2 platinum, split 403.
Report: Syntax Report.  This command reports your condition to the room.
Assist: If you do not have auto-assist on, you can type Assist <player>
        to help them out in combat.
Config: See this option to turn on auto-assist, auto-loot, auto-split and
        many other useful options.

Get       <object> [<from this object>]
Put       <object> <goes in this object>

Give      <object/money> <player>
Examine   <object>                     - Examining gems will show their mana.

Recite    <Scroll name>
Quaff     <Potion name>
Zap       <target> <wand>
Brandish  <staff name>
Search    [<direction>] (searches room for items or for a hidden exit)
Hide      <object>
Compare   <object 1> <object 2>
Eat/Drink <object>                     -- See also help DRINK
Fill      <object> <source of liquid>  -- See also help FILL
Empty     <object>
Swap      (Switches items held in hands from primary to secondary, etc)

Sheath    <held weapon name>

Sacrifice <object on ground>

{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
ALIAS     - See HELP ALIAS.
SCORE     - Shows your current character status and info about your character.
INFO      - Shows information like Score, only with a more elegant output.
ATTRIBUTE - Shows information about your character's attributes.
AFFECTS   - Shows what you are currently affected by (ie Armor, Poison).
EQUIPMENT - Shows what you are wearing at the time.
INVENTORY - Shows what you are carrying in your inventory.
EXITS     - Shows the rooms around where you are, and which direction.
WIZLIST   - Shows info about the administration, see also HELP ORIN.
CONFIG    - Shows you options currently set.  Use Config <option> to toggle.
STORE     - Shows what equipment you have in the Bank storage.
CSTORE    - Shows what is in the clan storage locker.
WEIGHT    - Shows the weight you are carrying and how burdened you are.
SCAN      - Scans all around you, checking for players or mobs.
SPELLS    - Shows the spells you know, their mana type and mana.
SKILLS    - Shows what skills you know, and how well you know them.
LEVEL     - Shows you how much experience is needed for each level.
WHO [nme] - Shows you who is currently playing the game.
TOPTEN    - Shows the top ten good/evil killers in the world.
TROPHY    - Shows your best kills of the opposite alignment.
COMMANDS  - Shows you a list of all the commands in the game.
SOCIALS   - Shows you a list of all the social commands in the game.
GLANCE    - Syntax is Glance <player>.  This shows the player's condition
            without the player knowing you are looking at him/her.
WEATHER   - Shows the current weather in the room you are in (not always
            accurate though.)
CLAN      - Shows information about your clan if you belong to one.
WORLD     - Shows how long the mud has been up, along with some statistics.
TIME      - Shows the current game time and day.
PLAYER    - Shows several bits of information regarding players.
RATING    - This shows the top ten rated players, and your rating.
EVENTS    - This shows the recent and upcoming events (quests, etc...)
CHANGES   - This shows the complete list of recent changes to the code.
CONSIDER  - Considers a one on one battle with the target mob.
RESULT #  - This will show you the result of voting question #.  If no
            number is specified, all the voting topics will be listed.
GCONSIDER - Considers how your group would do against a target.  See
            help GCONSIDER for more information on how this works.
FINGER    - Syntax is FINGER <player>.  This will show information about
            the specified player.  The player need not be online.

MINMANA <spellname> - This command shows the minimum mana <spellname> will require.

MANA [level] <spellname> - This command shows how much <spellname> will cost
                           at level [level].

0 LEARN LEARNS LEARNING~
Syntax: learn
Syntax: learn <skill|spell>

Learn is a command which allows you to learn a skill/spell.  Learned
skills/spells must then be practiced.

'Learn' without any arguments will display all the skills/spells that you
may learn from the mob in the room, if any.

Each learn requires a learn session.  To learn a skill, you use up a learn
session.  Type 'learn <skill or spell name>' to learn a new skill/spell.

You must find guildmasters/practitioners that teach certain skills/spells.

See Also: PRACTICE
~

101 ADVANCING~
If you want to become a more involved immortal, contact one of the level 109
or 110 immortals and ask them what information you can obtain on become a
higher level immortal.  They will tell you: There is no possible way,
just stay out of mortal's affairs and you may find youself a higher immort.
~

0 DEATH~
When your character dies, you are reincarnated, you don't die permanately.
Your corpse is left behind in the room where you were killed, together with
all of your equipment and gold.  Corpses are SAVED OVER REBOOTS and do
not appear until you enter the world again.  Abuse of this feature will
result in character deletion or removal of items.

1) Any spells which were affecting you are canceled by death.
2) You lose experience points for dying.  When you die, the experience points
   you lose are based on your total exp points.  You can never lose a
   level from death.  You also lose all yer equipment which is usually
   the toughest aspect of dying.  Experience loss is much lower for
   player kills than for mobdeath.
3) You can die if you don't eat or drink.
4) You will be transported to a certain hall of ressurection depending on
   your alignment and/or race.

Corpses decay after time, but in players' corpses, objects do not decay
with the corpse.  LOOTING OF CORPSES IS FINE!  Just make sure the guy
doesn't have 10 friends ready to beat you up if you loot his corpse!
Player corpses last *roughly* 30 hours of game time (30 minutes of real time)
unless they are looted, in which case they only last 1 game hour.
~

0 EXPERIENCE LEVEL XP EXP LEVELS~
Your character advances in power by gaining experience.  You need a varying
amount of experience points for each level of experience.  To find out how
much you need for the next level, use the 'score' command.

You gain experience every time you hit a mob or player and do damage,
when you cast an offensive spell that damages a player or mob, and when
you kill a monster or are part of a group that kills a monster.

You lose experience by dying, and a small bit from fleeing.

Experience awarded by mobs varies depending on how many have been killed,
their level, their extra bonuses, etc.  Help GBONUS for group experience
division.  Sometimes barons or gods will sponsor or help you out when you
gain levels, but this is not a common occurance.

Type 'level' for a list of experience needed for each level.
~

0 !~
Syntax: !

! repeats the last command you typed.
~

0 NORTH SOUTH EAST WEST UP DOWN ENTER CLIMB RUN~
Syntax: north
Syntax: south
Syntax: east
Syntax: west
Syntax: up
Syntax: down
Syntax: climb [up/down] <object>
Syntax: run <direction> [count]
Syntax: enter <object>

Use these commands to walk in a particular direction.

CLIMB is used to climb objects that are climbable.  If the object can be
climbed either up or down, you must give a direction.  Otherwise, no
direction is necessary.

RUN will move you in a direction until you can't move in that direction
no more.  Or you can give a count of how many spaces to move.  Running
will take more movements off and prevent you from doing anything while
running.

ENTERing objects will allow you into some special places.
~

0 FLY LAND~
Syntax: fly
Syntax: land

FLY will enable Dragonkins to fly and any other characters to fly on demand
if they have the 'fly' affect spell casted on them.

LAND will enable anyone to stop flying and land on the ground.

You may land and fly whenever you want as long as you have the 'fly' spell
casted on you or you are a Dragonkin race which inherits 'fly' at start.
~

0 LIGHT EXTINGUISH~
Syntax: light      <light object>
Syntax: extinguish <light object>

Lighting a lightable object can only be done with a tinderbox tool.
Extinguishing a lightable objects puts out the light on demand.
~

0 CAST~
Syntax: cast <spell> <target>

Before you can cast a spell, you have to practice it.  The more you practice,
the higher chance you have of success when casting.  Casting spells costs mana.
The mana cost decreases as your level increases.

The <target> is optional.  Many spells which need targets will use an
appropriate default target, especially during combat.

If the spell name is more than one word, then you must quote the spell name.
Example: cast 'cure critic' frag.  Quoting is optional for single-word spells.
You can abbreviate the spell name.

When you cast an offensive spell, the victim usually gets a saving throw.
The effect of the spell is reduced or eliminated if the victim makes the
saving throw successfully.

See also the help sections for MAGIC, and also please read HELP MANA.
~

0 EXITS~
Syntax: exits

Tells you the visible exits of the room you are in.  Not all exits are visible.
~

0 DROP GET GIVE PUT TAKE~
Syntax: drop <object>
Syntax: drop <amount> coins
Syntax: get  <object>
Syntax: get  <object> <container>
Syntax: give <object> <character>
Syntax: give <amount> coins <character>
Syntax: put  <object> <container>

DROP drops an object, or some coins, on the ground.

GET gets an object, either lying on the ground, or from a container, or even
from a corpse.  TAKE is a synonym for get.

GIVE gives an object, or some coins, to another character.

PUT puts an object into a container.

DROP, GET and PUT understand the object names 'ALL' for all objects and
'ALL.object' for all objects with the same name.
~

0 EQUIPMENT INVENTORY~
Syntax: equipment
Syntax: inventory

EQUIPMENT lists your equipment (armor, weapons, and held items).
INVENTORY lists your inventory.

~

0 COMPARE~
Syntax: compare <object-1> <object-2>
Syntax: compare <object>

COMPARE compares two objects in your inventory.  If both objects are weapons,
it will report the one with the better average damage.  If both objects are
armor, it will report the one with the better armor class.

COMPARE with one argument compares an object in your inventory to the object
you are currently wearing or wielding of the same type.

COMPARE doesn't consider any special modifiers of the objects.
~

0 BACKSTAB BS DISARM KILL~
Syntax: backstab <character>
Syntax: disarm
Syntax: kill     <character>

KILL starts a fight, and, hopefully, kills something.  BACKSTAB is another way
to start a fight, used if you have learned the backstab skill.  BS is a
synonym for BACKSTAB.

DISARM is an auxiliary fighting command to disarm your opponent.

In order to BACKSTAB or DISARM successfully, you must practice
the appropriate skill.
~

0 SCAN~
Syntax: scan

Allows you to scan all the possible directions and look into them.
Similar to 'look' but shows you all possible directions not just the one.

See Also: LOOK
~

0 PRAY~
Syntax: pray <message you want to say to the Gods>

Allows you to communicate to the Gods.
Gets you a faster response from the Gods than any other known channel.

~

0 FLEE ASSIST RESCUE~
Syntax: flee
Syntax: rescue <character>
Syntax: assist <character>

Once you start a fight, you can't just walk away from it.  If the fight
is not going well, you can attempt to FLEE, or another character can
RESCUE you.

If you lose your link during a fight, then your character will keep
fighting, and will attempt to FLEE from time to time.

In order to RESCUE successfully, you must practice the appropriate skill.

You may ASSIST someone at any time.  You will begin to help fighting.
~

0 EXAMINE LOOK~
Syntax: look
Syntax: look    <object>
Syntax: look    <character>
Syntax: look    <direction>
Syntax: look    <keyword>
Syntax: look in <container>
Syntax: look in <corpse>
Syntax: examine <container>
Syntax: examine <corpse>
Syntax: examine <gem>

LOOK looks at something and sees what you can see.

EXAMINE is short for 'LOOK container' followed by 'LOOK IN container'.

Examining GEMS will show you the mana left available to use.

Use: look <direction>      shows you what mobs are in a specific direction
~

0 ORDER~
Syntax: order <character> command
Syntax: order all command

ORDER orders one or all of your charmed followers (including pets) to
perform any command.  The command may have arguments.  You are responsible
for the actions of your followers, and others who attack your followers
will incur the same penalty as if they attacked you directly.

Most charmed creatures lose their aggresive nature (while charmed).

If your charmed creature engages in combat, that will break the charm.
~

0 REST SLEEP STAND WAKE~
Syntax: rest
Syntax: sleep
Syntax: stand
Syntax: wake

These commands change your position.  When you REST or SLEEP, you
regenerate hit points, mana points, and movement points faster.
However, you are more vulnerable to attack, and if you SLEEP,
you won't hear many things happen.

Use STAND or WAKE to come back to a standing position.  You can
also WAKE other sleeping characters.
~

0 GTELL ; SAY LISTEN REPLY TELL~
Syntax: gtell <message>
Syntax: say   <message>
Syntax: listen <character | all>
Syntax: reply <message>
Syntax: tell  <character> <message>

All of these commands send messages to other players.  GTELL sends a message to
all of the characters in your group, wherever they are, even if they are
sleeping or stunned or dying.  ';' is a synonym for GTELL.

SAY sends a message to all awake players in your room.  The single quote '''
is a synonym for SAY.

LISTEN allows only the character you select to be heard in the same room.
This is useful for holding conversations with one person in a crowded
room with lots of people SAYing, without having to use TELL.
LISTEN all will turn off LISTENing.

TELL sends a message to one awake player anywhere in the world.

REPLY sends a message to the last player who sent you a TELL.  REPLY will work
even if you can't see the player, and without revealing their identity.  This
is handy for talking to invisible or switched immortal players.
~

0 NOTE~
Syntax: note list
Syntax: note write
Syntax: note read    <number>
Syntax: note read    all
Syntax: note subject <string>
Syntax: note to      <to-list>
Syntax: note clear
Syntax: note send
Syntax: note show
Syntax: note post
Syntax: note remove  <number>
Syntax: note wipe    <name>  or <start note number> <end note number> LEVEL 111 only. <mortals> 111 only.

NOTE LIST lists notes which you can read.  NOTE READ reads one or all notes.

NOTE WRITE will start the online text editor so you can enter a note easier
than using note +.

NOTE SUBJECT sets the subject line of a new note.  NOTE TO sets the list of
recipients.  The recipient ALL means all players, and the recipient IMMORTAL
means all immortals.  Use NOTE + to write message lines onto the note, one line
at a time.  NOTE SHOW shows your note in progress; NOTE CLEAR starts over.

NOTE POST or NOTE SEND posts your note for reading.  Posting is not automatic.

NOTE REMOVE removes the entire note if you are the sender, or just removes you
from the to-list if you are a recipient.
~

0 AUCTION GOSSIP GOS QUESTION ANSWER SHOUT YELL CHAT~
Syntax: auction  <message>
Syntax: gossip   <message>
Syntax: question <message>
Syntax: answer   <message>
Syntax: shout    <message>
Syntax: yell     <message>
Syntax: chat     <message>

These commands send messages through communication channels to other players.

SHOUT sends a message to all awake players in the world.  To curb excessive
shouting, SHOUT imposes a three-second delay on the shouter.

GOSSIP, and QUESTION and ANSWER also send messages to all
interested players.  '.' is a synonym for GOSSIP.  The QUESTION and ANSWER
commands both use the same 'question' channel

YELL sends a message to all awake players within your area.

You can use the CHANNELS command to hear, or not hear, any of these channels.

See Also: PRAY
~

0 GRAB HOLD REMOVE WEAR WIELD~
Syntax: hold   <object>
Syntax: grab   <object>
Syntax: remove <object>
Syntax: wear   <object>
Syntax: wear   all
Syntax: wield  <object>

Three of these commands will take an object from your inventory and start using
it as equipment.  HOLD is for light sources, wands, and staves.  WEAR is for
armor.  WIELD is for weapons.

WEAR ALL will attempt to HOLD, WEAR, or WIELD each suitable item in your
inventory.

You may not be able to HOLD, WEAR, or WIELD an item if its alignment does not
match yours, if it is too heavy for you, or if you are not experienced enough
to use it properly.

REMOVE will take any object from your equipment and put it back into your
inventory.
~

0 CHANNELS~
Syntax: channels
Syntax: channels +<channel>
Syntax: channels -<channel>

With no options, CHANNELS shows you your current channels.  With a plus or
minus sign and an option, CHANNELS turns that channel on or off.
~

0 CONFIG~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                            {R}Config
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}

Syntax: config
Syntax: config  <option>

This command configures some of your character behavior.  With no options,
CONFIG shows you your current settings.  With a plus or minus sign and
an option, CONFIG turns that option on or off.  CONFIG <option> alone
toggles the option on or off.

Some options are:

[ upprompt  ] If you have mapping on, the prompt will be down.
[ AUTOEXIT  ] You automatically see exits.
[ AUTOLOOT  ] You automatically loot corpses.
[ AUTOSAC   ] You automatically sacrifice corpses.
[ AUTOGOLD  ] You automatically loot coins from corpses.
[ AUTOSPLIT ] You automatically split coins looted from corpses.
[ ASSIST    ] You automatically assist your group in combat.
[ floatbot  ] Bottom-Floating prompt is off.
[ floattop  ] Top-Floating prompt is off.
[ BLANK     ] You have a blank line before your prompt.
[ brief     ] You see long descriptions.
[ COMBINE   ] You see object lists in combined format.
[ PROMPT    ] You have a prompt.
[ ANSI      ] You receive ansi color codes.
[ CHALLNGE  ] You allow arena challenges from other players.
[ ARENA     ] You will see updated status of arena battles.
[ EqlisT    ] Equipment is sorted, all slots are shown.

~

See: AUTOLOOT, AUTOEXIT, AUTOASSIST, AUTOSAC, AUTOGOLD, AUTOSPLIT

deal the final blow.

See CONFIGURE to find out which toggle is on and which is off.

AUTOEXIT toggles your ability to automatically see exits as you enter
a room.

See CONFIGURE to find out which toggle is on and which is off.
~

0 AUTOSAC~
Syntax: autosac

AUTOSAC toggles your ability to automatically sacrifice corpses after
you deal the final blow.

See CONFIGURE to find out which toggle is on and which is off.
~

0 BLANK~
Syntax: blank

BLANK toggles existance of a blank before your prompt.

See CONFIGURE to find out which toggle is on and which is off.
~

0 AREAS COMMANDS SOCIALS~
Syntax: areas
Syntax: commands
Syntax: socials

AREAS shows you all the areas in the game, with the author's name and the
suggested levels.

COMMANDS shows you all the (non-social) commands available to you.

SOCIALS shows you all the social commands available to you.
~

0 BRIEF~
Syntax: brief

BRIEF allows you to not see the room descriptions in the rooms so you will
get less scroll when you move quickly.

Typing 'brief' again will toggle back to seeing room descriptions.
~

0 WHERE~
Syntax: where
Syntax: where <character>

WHERE without an argument tells you the location of visible players of the
same alignment (good and neutral rolled into one, evil is seperate) in the
same area as you are.

WHERE with an argument tells you the location of one character with that name
within your area.

WHERE will not show oppositely aligned characters or mobiles.  The where
command will also show which zone you are currently in.
~

0 DESCRIPTION~
Syntax: description <string>
Syntax: description + <string>

Sets your long description to the given string.  If the description string
starts with a '+', the part after the '+' is appended to your current
description, so that you can make multi-line descriptions.
~

0 PASSWORD~
Syntax: password <old-password> <new-password>

PASSWORD changes your character's password.  The first argument must be
your old password.  The second argument is your new password.

The PASSWORD command is protected against being snooped or logged.
~

0 TITLE~
Syntax: title <string>
Syntax: title <colorcodes/title>$N

Sets your title to a given string.

The game supplies a title when your character is created and when you
advance a level.  You can use TITLE to set your title to something else.

COLOR CODES TO SET YOUR TITLE

{g}$N$1 {b}Blue{g}         {g}$N$5 {p}Purple       {g}$B Bold
{g}$B$1 {B}Blue{g}         $B$5 {P}Purple
{g}$N$2 {g}Green{g}        $N$6 {y}Yellow       {g}$I Inverse
{g}$B$2 {G}Green{g}        $B$6 {Y}Yellow
{g}$N$3 {c}Cyan{g}         $N$7 {w}Grey         {g}$F Flashing (don't use too much please)
{g}$B$3 {C}Cyan{g}         $B$7 {W}White
{g}$N$4 {r}Red{g}          $B$0 {d}Dark Grey    {g}$R Normal (sets color to default)
{g}$B$4 {R}Red{g}          
To color your title:
example: title $1is here$N   The 'is here' is Blue.  $N sets back to normal.
example: title $4red$B$7white$1blue$R sets red to red, white to white, etc.

See Also: COLOR, ANSI
~

0 CONFIGURATION 'CONFIGURATION COMMANDS'~
Config  : This shows options.  Toggle on and off by using Config <option>.
Pagelen : This sets how long your page length is.  Syntax is Pagelen #.
Wimpy   : See help WIMPY.
Channel : This shows what communication channels you are listening to.  Use
          Channel -<channelname> or Channel +<channelname> to turn off/on.
Spam    : Use this command to toggle levels of spam.  See help SPAM.
Fight   : Use this command to see the attitudes of how your character
          fights.  Use Fight <option> to toggle a fight option.

~

0 WIMPY~
Syntax: wimpy
Syntax: wimpy <number>

WIMPY sets your wimpy value.  When your character takes damage that reduces
your hit points below your wimpy value, you will automatically attempt to flee.

WIMPY with no argument sets your wimpy value to 20.

Some monsters are wimpy.


~

0 OPEN CLOSE LOCK UNLOCK PICK~
Syntax: open   <object|direction>
Syntax: close  <object|direction>
Syntax: lock   <object|direction>
Syntax: unlock <object|direction>
Syntax: pick   <object|direction>

OPEN and CLOSE open and close an object or a door.

LOCK and UNLOCK lock and unlock a closed object or door.  You must have
the requisite key to LOCK or UNLOCK.

PICK can open a lock without having the key.  In order to PICK successfully,
you must practice the appropriate skill.
~

0 DRINK EAT FILL EMPTY~
Syntax: drink <object>
Syntax: eat   <object>
Syntax: fill  <object>
Syntax: empty <object>

When you are thirsty, DRINK something.

When you are hungry, EAT something.

FILL fills a drink container with water.

When you wish to EMPTY a drink container of its liquids.
~

0 SHOP BUY LIST SELL VALUE 'SHOP COMMANDS'~
Syntax: buy   <object>
Syntax: list  <object>
Syntax: sell  <object>
Syntax: value <object>

BUY buys an object from a shop keeper.

LIST with no argument lists the objects the shop keeper will sell you.
LIST <object> lists only the items corresponding with <object> the shop
keeper will sell you.

SELL sells an object to a shop keeper.

VALUE asks the shop keeper how much he, she, or it will buy the item for.
~

0 SACRIFICE~
Syntax: sacrifice <object>

SACRIFICE offers an object to your God.  A Sacrifice is a Sacrifice;
don't expect any lousy steenken coins or anything.
~

0 TAP BRANDISH QUAFF RECITE ZAP~
Syntax: brandish
Syntax: quaff    <potion>
Syntax: recite   <scroll> <target>
Syntax: zap      <target>
Syntax: tap

BRANDISH brandishes a magical staff.  QUAFF quaffs a magical potion (as opposed
to DRINK, which drinks mundane liquids).  RECITE recites a magical scroll; the
<target> is optional, depending on the nature of the scroll.  ZAP zaps a
magical wand at a target.  If the target is not specified, and you are fighting
someone, then that character is used for a target.

You must HOLD a wand or a staff before using BRANDISH or ZAP.

All of these commands use up their objects.  Potions and scrolls have a single
charge.  Wands and staves have multiple charges.  When a magical object has no
more charges, it will be consumed.
~

0 SHEATH DRAW~
Syntax: sheath <weapon>
Syntax: draw   <weapon>

Sheath will allow you to place a weapon into your belt for future use.

Draw will remove any sheathed weapons from your belt for you to use.

~

0 GCONSIDER~
Syntax: gconsider <victim>

This command shows you how well your group would do against a mob if
you were taking the hits.  It is best if the would-be "tank" or "buffer"
uses this command, as it will be the most accurate.  Only group members
actually in the room with the mob will be used in the gconsider command.

See also: CONSIDER
~

0 CONSIDER~
Syntax: consider <victim>

CONSIDER tells you what your chances are of killing a character.
Of course, it's only a rough estimate.

See also: GCONSIDER
~

0 GBONUS~
First of all, I would like to state that the reason for grouping is NOT
to gain mucho exp fast (although it CAN be done in a very good,
fast-moving group).  The main purpose of grouping is hunting, safety, and
equipment hunting.  Enough of the blabber.. here are the equations:

experience each member gets = (MOB_EXP * (1+(members/10))) / members

There are slight bonuses for killing higher level mobs with smaller groups.
With this equation, you can see a group of 15 gets 2.5 times the mob
experience, only it is divided by 15.  A group of two gets 1.2 times the
mob experience, divided by two, plus a small "small-group" bonus
depending on the level mob they kill.

~

0 FOLLOW GROUP~
Syntax: follow <character>
Syntax: group
Syntax: group <character> or ALL

TYPE HELP GBONUS to find out about GROUP BONUSES, exp division, etc...

FOLLOW starts you following another character.  To stop following anyone else,
just FOLLOW <yourself>.

GROUP <character> makes someone who is following you a member of your group.
Group members share experience points from kills and may use the GTELL and
SPLIT commands.  If anyone in your group is attacked, you will automatically
join the fight if you have autoassist on.

If the <character> is already a member of your group, then GROUP will
kick out the <character> from your group.  Characters can also leave your
group by using a FOLLOW command to stop following you.

GROUP with no argument shows statistics for each character in your group.
~

0 HIDE SNEAK VISIBLE~
Syntax: HIDE
Syntax: SNEAK
Syntax: VISIBLE

If you type HIDE <object> you will hide an object in the room.
Other people in the room will see you hiding it, so be warned.

If you type HIDE along (nothing after it):
If you successfully HIDE, then other characters can't see you.

If you successfully SNEAK, then you can move in and out of rooms without
being noticed.

In order to HIDE or SNEAK successfully, you must practice the appropriate
skill.

VISIBLE cancels your hiding and sneaking, as well as any invisibility,
making you visible again.

SEE ALSO: SEARCH
~

0 QUIT RENT SAVE~
Syntax: QUIT

 Some objects, such as keys and potions, may not be saved.

QUIT leaves the game.  When you re-enter the game you will be back in the
same room you quit in.

QUIT automatically does a SAVE, so you can safely leave the game with just one
command.

There is no RENT in this mud.  Just SAVE and QUIT whenever you want to leave.
However, you may find that you cannot quit immediately after combat; this is
so that you may not quit to avoid being chased after.
~

0 SPLIT~
Syntax: SPLIT <amount>

SPLIT splits some gold between you and all the members of your
group who are in the same room as you.  It's customary to SPLIT
the gold after a kill.
~

0 PRACTITIONER 'PRACTITIONER COMMANDS'~
See help PRACTICE, and help LEARN, help SLIST.

Skills will show you the skills you know, while Spells shows you the
spells you know and how much mana they cost at your current level.
Slist spells shows you all the spells in the game, Slist skills shows
you all the skills in the game.  There may be several hidden spells
and skills though.

~

0 PRACTICE~
Syntax: PRACTICE
Syntax: PRACTICE <skill|spell>

PRACTICE without an argument tells you your current ability level in all
the skills and spells available to you.  You can check this anywhere.

PRACTICE with an argument practice that skill or spell.  Your learning
percentage varies from 0% (unlearned) to a some maximum between 80% and 100%,
depending on your race.  You must be at a guild master to practice.

The higher your intelligence, the more you will learn at each practice
session.  The higher your wisdom, the more practice sessions you will
have each time you gain a level.  Unused sessions are saved until you
do use them.

You must find a guildmaster or practitioner that teaches skills/spells.

See Also: LEARN
~

0 READ~
Syntax: read <object>

Allows you to read certain writing or descriptions on objects.
~

0 MOUNT DISMOUNT RIDE~
Syntax: mount    <mountable>
Syntax: dismount <mountable>
Syntax: ride     <mountable>

Allows you to mount, dismount, or ride mountable mobiles.
Mounting mobiles will not use any of your moves, but will tire the mounted.
~

101 BeemIN BeemOUT~
Syntax: beemin  <message>
Syntax: beemout <message>

The standard messages for GOTO are 'arrives in a swirling mist' and
'leaves in a swirling mist'.  You can replace these messages with messages of
your own choosing using the BAMFIN and BAMFOUT commands.
~

102 SLOOKUP~
Syntax: slookup <skill-or-spell>
Syntax: slookup all

SLOOKUP shows you the internal 'sn' and external 'slot' for the given skill
or spell.  The 'sn' is used for OSET and OSTAT.  The 'slot' is used for area
files.  Neither 'sn' nor 'slot' is used for player files; these operate with
the actual skill and spell names.

SLOOKUP ALL shows this information for all skills and spells.
~

0 SKILLS~
Syntax: skills

This command shows the skills you know as well as how good you are at them.

For a list of ALL available skills for your race, type HELP SLIST.
~

0 SPELLS~
Syntax: spells

This command shows the spell caster how much mana each spell he knows will
cost.

For a list of ALL available spells for your race, type HELP SLIST.
~

slist spells : will show you the spells available

0 PAGELENGTH PAGE PAGER~
Syntax: pagelength
Syntax: pagelength <number>

Pagelength without an argument sets the number of lines before page
pause to the default of 20 lines.

Pagelength with an argument sets the number of lines you wish to see on
screen before page pausing.

For more help on the pager, type 'h' while in the pager.

0 PROMPT~
PROMPT COMMANDS
*20n* = Left justify name, pad 20 chars.
*a*  = age.
*n*  = name.
*t*  = title.
*r*  = race.
*#g* = goto x pos.
*pt* = playing time.
*ap* = Attack power bonus.
*eb* = Evasion bonus.
*ob* = Offensive bonus.
*al* = Alignment.
*hn* = hp now.
*hm* = hp max.
*hw* = hp word.
*mn* = mv now.
*mm* = mv max.
*mw* = mv word.
*xl* = exp to level.
*tl* = tps to level.
*xp* = total exp.
*kw* = Kilograms of weight.
*ww* = Word weight rating.
*cn* = Coins carrying.
*cb* = Coins in bank.
*ht* = Height.
*cr* = Carrying #.
*tc* = Total Kills.
*kp* = Kill Points.
*wp* = Warpoints
*tp* = Travel points.
*mnn*= mana now (numeric).
*mmm*= mana max (numeric).
*wm* = word mana.
*lvl*= Level.
*wim*= Wimpy.
*pos*= Position.  Use this on previous line.
*aff*= current effects.  Use this on previous line.
*cond* = Condition now.  Use this on previous line.
*clan* = In clan (if any).  Use this on previous line.
*guil* = In guild (if any).  Use this on previous line.
*warm* = Warmth (if any).  Use this on previous line.
*fi*   = Fighting opponent condition
*tk*   = Tank condition

PROMPT ALL will reset to the default prompt.

An example would be:
$B$1*hn*/*hm*$R$7hp $B$2*mn*/*mm*$R$7mv $B$3*mnn*/*mmm*$R$7m $B$5(*xl*)$R$7xp $B$7*fi* *tk*$R>

This would show something like: 44/44hp 33/33mv 101/101m (230)xp [Opponent: Good]>

Also See HELP COLORS to see prompt color codes.

~

        *an* :  Display the area name you are in (IMMORTAL ONLY)

0 MANA~
Although each character has a certain amount of natural mana, spells
above level 10, and greater mana amounts can be achieved through the use
of GEMS.  Gems add mana, increase mana regneration rates, and allow you
to cast more powerful spells.  Natural mana regenerates VERY slowly.

Common gems that are sold in magic stores often cannot cast
higher level spells and hold less mana than less common, more powerful
gems.  Also, you cannot cast a spell like fireball with an earthen gem...
there are four types of gems and magic types: Earth, Air, Water, and
Fire.  Experiment around to see what spells use which or read the help on
each spell individually.  There are rumors of gems that can cast all
of the types of spells, but few mortals possess gems of this power.

See Also: GEMS, MAGIC, ELEMENTS

~

1 MAGIC~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                                   Magic
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
 
To cast spells, first you have to learn them.  Then practice makes perfect
when attempting to successfully cast.  Finally, the use of gems for the
empowering of spells is a must.
 
See Also: MANA, GEMS
~

0 GEMS~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                                     GEMS
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
Syntax: hold <gem>

Gems are the source of mana or magical energy needed to cast spells.  There
are (4) types of gems based on their elemental use.  Once you hold a gem
it begins to charge up for use.  There is a down side to this, as you will
be only left with 1 hand to fight with.

See Also: MAGIC, MANA, ELEMENTS

{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}

0 ELEMENT ELEMENTS 'THE ELEMENTS'~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                                      ELEMENTS
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
The elements are as follows:

EARTH
Nature, the earth, controls mending and binding magicks.  The earth shields
and heals.  It is the element of earth that holds the most powerful healing
spells, and it is also this element which can be used to thwart dangerous
foes.

AIR
Air controls travel and visibility, twisting and bending lights and shadow.
Air conceals, and it also can forcefully move like the winds of powerful
storms.

FIRE
Fire allows the unseen to glow brightly, to light the darkest room and to
burn harshly the most evil.  Fire allows a person to see the truth behind
the dark shrouds that covertly conceal many.

WATER
Water, the cleansing spirit, dominates and overcomes with unfolding strength.
It is a holy thing, coveted and used to help cure the sickest and vilest of
diseases, whether those diseases be plagues of the heart or of the mind.

DEATH
Death allows Necromancers to raise corpses, cast hexes, and attack spells.
This type of mana is only used by Necromancers and is worthless to any 
other class.

~

102 SCRIPT~
Scripts are divided into LABELS of code (code chunks) and TRIGGERS.
Triggers call a code chunk, and are activated at a set time (which you set).

To edit a code chunk, use EDIT CREATE <name>, or EDIT <name>.
Code chunk names can only be up to 10 letters long.

To type in your code, precede all lines with a :1, :2, :3, etc... as line
numbers.  You may insert something before line two just by typing :2 stuff to
insert.  To clear a line, type .c <ln>.  If you forgot some line numbers,
type .f to format it and make it look pretty.

to list all triggers, type listtrig
to list all code chunks, type listcode

Inside the code:
Code is basically interpretted by what is calling it "as is".  There are
some special functions though:

@P              Substitute the person who triggered the script's name here
@M              Substitute the mob who is running the script's name here
@O              Substitute the object who is running the script's short desc
@V              Substitues the vnum (object if obj, room if room, mob if mob)
@R(min,max)     Random number between min and max.

@Cx             character stat reference... here are the currently supported
                ones:  (NOTE they ARE case sensitive)

                        e = 1 if evil, 0 if good
                        g = 1 if good, 0 if evil
                        l = character's level

                eg: if @Cl>=10 then (read as: if level >= 10 then)

GOTO <ln>       jumps to a line number in that code chunk
CALL <label>    jumps to another code chunk/label
RECHO           echos something to the room.
WAIT <x> <type> where <x> is the number of ticks.  <type> is one of these:
                superquick : fastest pulse, about 3 per second
                quick      : a tick is about 1 second with quick
                heart      : a tick is the length of a heartbeat (regen)
                hour       : the wait is a full game hour
DONE            ends the script here and then, wherever it is encountered
CREATE_MOB <v>  where <v> is the vnum of the mob to create.
CREATE_OBJ <v>  where <v> is the vnum of the obj to create.
DESTROY_OBJ <v> where <v> is the vnum of the obj to destroy.
DESTROY_OBJ     with no arguments, if it's an object script, destroys the
                object upon which the script is running and ends script.

IF              This is a powerful command, but you must know how to work it.
                You may compare two numbers using ==, >=, <=, >, <, or !=

                You may compare two strings using == and !=

                You can do things such as: IF @R(1,3)==2 then

IF (flag)       This checks if the given flag is set on the character
IF (!flag)      This chekcs if the given flag is NOT set on the character

IF is followed by a " then", and nothing else on the line.
If the statement is TRUE, then the NEXT LINE, and the NEXT LINE ONLY! get
executed.  This is in the style of assembly language.  You CANNOT use {} like
in C.  This makes GOTO and CALL very important.

examples:

:1 if @R(1,3)!=2 then
:2 call not_two
:3 say the number was equal to 2!

..or..

:1 if (!OR2) then
:2 goto 5
:3 say You have the orin 2 flag on, btw.
:4 done
:5 say You don't have the or2 flag on!! setting it to on!
:6 pset @P scriptflag OR2 on

..or..

:1 if @P==Orin then
:2 echo Orin is in the house everybody!!
:3 done

---------------
Useful flags!!!
---------------
Note: Objects and rooms may only set things, etc.. they cannot "say" "tell",
etc... they can, however RECHO.

Flags are up to four letters long and are stored on the character.  To set
a flag, your script (or you can do it manually) should use:

pset playername scriptflag <sf> ON/OFF

Here are some examples:
pset @P scriptflag SF1 ON
pset @P scriptflag AAA OFF

Please note... 'clean up' script flags in scripts.. if you have temporary
script flags, make sure to have the flags cleared when the script is
complete, and make it so only a single "script complete" scriptflag is on.
There can be up to 3000 script flags stored on a character.  However, it
doesn't keep track... if you remove a script from the game, characters will
retain the 3 or 4 letter script flag identifiers on them.

Script flags can't overlap.. make sure to come up with some scheme.. for
insance god PALIO might use PA1 - PA99, and ORIN might use OR1 - OR99.

---------
Debugging
---------
Only ONE person may be in debugging mode at once.  To enter it, type DEBUG.
All error messages generated by scripts will be routed to you.

Important: You MUST asave triggers and asave code when you want to save your
work!!!!!!

----------
SCRIPTEDIT
----------
Format: scriptedit create <trigger_id> or scriptedit <trigger_id>

Each trigger has a unique ID which can be up to 20 letters in length.
Once in the trigger editor, press enter to see current info on the
current "script"/"trigger".

The current triggers CURRENTLY available are:
Trigger         When triggered          For (O)bjects (M)obs (R)ooms
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}--
ENTERS          When someone enters     M, R
LEAVES          When someone leaves     M, R
CREATED         When it resets          M
COMMAND         When player types       M, R
SAYS            When a player uses say  M, R
TELLS           When a player tells     M
EVERY_HOUR      Every game hour         M
EVERY_QUICKTICK Every second            M
EVERY_REGENTICK Every 5-6 seconds       M
GIVEN           When given object       OM
DROPPED         When dropped            OR

Keywords hold extra data.. for instance, the keywords:
'hello there' 'hello' 'greeting' 'hi'
would be used in conjunction with a SAY trigger to go off when a player
uses one of those expressions in his/her SAY command.  A blank keyword with
a say/tell field will trigger always when a player says/tells.

with given/dropped, keywords can hold a list of vnums to trigger on.
If blank, any vnum will do.  EG: if it's a mob script, keywords holds a list
of vnums the script will trigger on if the mob is given object vnum X.
If it's a object script, keywords holds a list of vnums of mobs the script
will trigger on if the obj is given to this mob.

Coming in the future: (possibly) GIVEN_MONEY, ON_DEATH, OBJ_SACCED

Other options in scriptedit:
----------------------------

CODE <code_chunk>       This is the code chunk which is "launched" when
                        your trigger goes off.
interrupt               this toggles whether or not the script can be
                        interrupted part way through with another trigger
                        instance.
stops                   In specific scripts (room/mob), if this is set
                        and the character leaves the room, the script ends.
player                  Player only.  If this is on, only players will be
                        able to trigger the script.  If not, mobs entering
                        the room and such can trigger it.
Room <vnum>
Mob <vnum>              These are the vnums the script is linked onto.
Obj <vnum>              Only ONE of these should be set!!

~

101 TRAPS 'IREF TRAPS'~
These traps can just be toggled on/off in a room like room-flags.  ONLY
USE ONE TRAP PER ROOM PLEASE!!

 firetrap       Flames rise up, doing 1-35 damage every 1-3 seconds
                Intelligence and dexterity can allow you to dodge the
                flames to an extent.
 rocktrap       Falling rocks fall at random times (1-7 seconds) on a
                victim's head.  His helmet can absorb the blows to an
                extent.  Without helmet it does 1-50 damage OUCH!
                Also, the victim's helmet will be damaged if it is metal
                (ie has a higher armor class).  Note: high dexterity and
                intelligence and wisdom may allow you to dodge the rocks.
 arrowtrap      This makes arrows shoot "out of nowhere" to hit the victim.
                Arrows are dodgeable and victim's armor makes a difference.
                Dodge depents on intelligence and dexterity. 1-30 dam
 poisontrap     Exactly like above but if hit, you will be poisoned for
                1-10 hours.  If poisoned, it will add 1 hour for each time
                you get hit.
 gastrapone     This can be used for swamps and sewers.  Does 1-4 damage
                ocassionally and cannot be dodged or saved against.
 gastraptwo     A much meaner version of gastrapone.  It does 1-35 damage
                and poisons the victim.  If victim is poisoned, it adds
                1 hour to duration.
 spiketrap      Players sometimes fall on spikes and get damaged (spikes
                should be in the room description to use this trap!
 avalanche      NOTE: An avalance only goes off once!  It does enormous
                damage, and therefore it is recommended that an avalanche
                room be set to no_mobs, so wandering mobs don't trigger it.
 manadrain      This room drains mana when you stand in it (the gem
                the victim is holding).
 gysertrap      This will make it so a spray of scalding hot water hits
                its victim, doing a good amount of damage.  Make sure
                you put in your room description about something that
                could do such a thing, like a gyser.  Otherwise this trap
                won't make much sense.

110 AEDIT 'IREF AEDIT'~
AEDIT alone enters the AREA editor.

The follow commands are available from within the AEDITOR:

show                - hitting return, or 'show' shows the area stats
done                - exits the area editor and returns to normal play
create              - create a brand new area and switch to it
name <name>         - change the 'AREAS' name of this area
filename <filename> - change the file name for the area (be careful)
age <number>        - set the age of the area
recall <room vnum>  - set the room to recall to
repop               - set the repop string (shown when a area is reset)
security <rating>   - set the security rating for this area
builder <player>    - toggle that builder's access

See Also:  ASTAT, AREAS, RESETS, MFIND, OFIND, RFIND, COUNT
~

101 redit 'room editor'~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                               {R}ROOM EDITOR
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
{N}Redit is a powerful editor which allows for creation of rooms, creating exits,
linking together rooms, setting traps, ect. To enter the room editor, use REDIT. 
No vnum is specified after redit; You must be in the room you wish to edit. To create
a blank room to edit, you can use redit create <vnum>. However, in most cases the 
DIG command is easier (explained below). First of all, use flaglist to see available 
flags in any editor, including redit!

 

{R}REDIT COMMANDS
 

{G}Done                                  Quits the editor.

{B}<ENTER>                               Shows info on the current room.

{G}Name                                  Sets the rooms name.

{B}Desc                                  Enters the rooms description (make sure you are in redit 
                                      other wise you will end up putting the description on 
                                      your characters description)

{G}}                                     go to the next vnum {R}(GOD ONLY)

{B}SH                                    Marks the room as SHADED

{G}LI                                    Light cancels Shade (this is the default of rooms)

{B}Copyto <vnum>                         Copies the room description in the current room TO the 
                                       specified room vnum.

{G}Copyfrom <vnum>                       Copies the room description in the current room FROM the 
                                       specified room vnum.

{B}Nameto <vnum>                         Copies the current room name and sector type TO the 
                                       specified room vnum.

{G}Namefrom <vnum>                       Copies the current room name and sector type FROM the
                                       specified room vnum.

{B}ED ADD <keyword>                      This adds certain descriptive things to a room. For 
				       instance: ed add statue large granite will allow me to
				       edit the description if a person looks at statue large 
                                       granite.

{G}ED EDIT <keyword>                     This allows you to edit a descriptive thing already in the
			               room. To edit the large statue, I would type: ed edit 
                                       statue. (not statue large granite).

{B}ED DELETE <keyword>                   This allows you to delete the descriptive thing already
                                       existing in the room. To delete the large statue, I 
                                       would type: ed delete statue.

{G}ED FORMAT <keyword>                   Formats the description like .f in editor.

 

{R}This next section is on SECTORS and how each sector affects movement.

 

{g}To calculate movement loss, use the following equation.
(move cost of sector you are leaving) + (move cost of sector that you are entering) / 2
Or if you are flying:
(move cost of sector you are leaving) + (move cost of sector that you are entering) / 3

Then....
Add 1 if you are carrying > (strength*2)
Add 1 more if you are carrying > (strength*3)
Add 2 more if you are carrying > (strength*4)
Add 3 more if you are carrying > (strength*5)
Add 4 more if you are carrying > (strength*6)

Add 1 if the player has no shoes on.

Divide this number by 2 if easier_moves is on in power.dat.

To set a rooms SECTOR, simply type the sector name in the desired room (while in redit).
Here is what each sector does.

 
{B}Inside           1 move        This room to be covered. Marked as always lit. (ie. Shop, ect)
{G}City             2 moves       city or road. Easy going.
{B}Field            2 moves       Easy traveling.
{G}Forest           3 moves       More difficult traveling.
{B}Hills            4 moves       Hilly/Mountainous terrain. Very difficult travel.
{G}Mountain         6 moves       Requires grappling device. No blood trails
{B}Swim             4 moves       needs swim skill. No blood trails.
{G}Noswim           n/a           Ocean or DEEP WATER. No blood trails.
{B}Underwater       6 moves       characters CAN drown here. No blood trails.
{G}Air              10 moves      You MUST be flying to travel in this sector. No blood trails.
{B}Desert           4 moves       Hotter then other sectors. Get thirsty faster. Blood
                               trails evaporate twice as fast in the desert.
{G}Snow             8/21 moves    Very tough going.
{B}Tropical         4 moves       Hotter then normal sectors. Tough going. No blood trails.
{G}Impassable       N/A           For use with java client. You cannot go into this room 
                               unless Holywalk is on.
{B}Ice              3 moves       No change in temp. but frozen surfaces. Moderately tough going.
{G}Marsh            3 moves       Swampy terrain. No blood trails.                     

{R}Ok now for the Best commands in Redit: the Direction Commands.

{B}<dir> delete                       Deletes the exit and link in the direction. Warning this 
                                   ONLY deletes ONE side making a one-way exit from the 
                                   other room!!!
{G}<dir> destroy                      Deletes BOTH the current exit and the opposite exit in the 
                                   room it is linked too.
{B}<dir> link <vnum>                  Links the current room to a pre-existing room <vnum> in the 
                                   direction specified (ie. West link 19485)
{G}<dir> dig <vnum>                   Creates a room and also links the room in the direction 
                                   you have specified. (ie. You are in room 100. You type 
                                   west dig 101. You have now created room 101 and made an 
                                   exit from 100 west into 101 and also from room 101 an 
                                   exit east back into room 100.)
{B}<dir> room <vnum>                 Creates a one-way link FROM the current room to the 
                                   room <vnum>
{G}<dir> desc                         Sets the description for the current exit. If the exit has 
                                   no link, this message will be displayed when someone bumps 
                                   into or looks at this direction. If this exit has a door 
                                   this is the description of the door.
{B}<dir> door                         Creates a door in this direction.
{G}<dir> closed                       Sets the default of this door to be closed.
{B}<dir> locked                       Sets the default of the door to be locked.
{G}<dir> pickproof                    Sets the door as unpick-able.
{B}<dir> hidden                       Sets the door as hidden, so that if the door is closed, 
                                   it wont be displayed on the exits readout. Does not work
                                   underwater.
{G}<dir> name <exit name>           This sets the doors name. For instance: west name door or 
                                 north name gatedoor. {R}** ONLY the door names with door as 
                                 the prefix or suffix can be broken!!!**
{B}<dir> str <strength>             Sets the strength of the door (if any) in the given direction. 
                                 A character with strength*2 can break a door of that strength. 
                                 For instance, a character with 24 strength could break up 
                                 to a (24*2)=48 strength door.
{G}<dir> key <obj vnum>             Sets the key to this door as object vnum <vnum>. 
                                 {R}Key vnums cannot exceed 32,000.

{R}Room FLAGS
 
{g}To toggle room flags on/off, simply type in the name of the flag while in redit.

 
{B}DARK                          This room in always dark (character needs a torch/infravision 
                              ect.. in he/she wants to see)
{G}NO_MOBS                       No mobs can enter this room. However, mobs can be created here; 
                              they just wont wander here.
{B}INDOORS                       Used often with inside sector. Marks the room to have 'a roof' 
                              or 'ceiling' aka.. indoors.
{G}PET_SHOP  {R}dont use{G}            This toggles this room as a pet shop room. If this room is vnum 
                              1501, vnum 1502 MUST be an isolated room where the mobs this room
                              will sell repop in.
{B}NOHEAR                        No yells can go through this room. I have seen with my mud that
                              this flag is used as the no recall flag. It might be a bug within
                              my code but I have no idea.
{G}NO_SUMMON                     You cannot be summoned from this room.
{B}UNTRACKABLE                   This room does not leave tracks of anyone who has passed through, 
                              nor can anyone scry anyone in this room.
{G}MOVING                        NEVER SET MANUALLY. See section on ROOM TRANSPORTS/CURRENTS.
{B}NOMAGIC                       No magic will function in this room.
{G}SILENCE                       Channels are blocked from use while in this room.
{B}EXTRAHEAL                     Characters heal faster while in this room.
{G}FALLFAST                      Use ONLY with AIR sector. Specifies non-flying characters can 
                              walk into this room, at which time they begin to fall down 
                              to the room(s) below.
{B}EXTRAMANA                     Characters regen mana faster while in this room. Often used 
                              with the EXTRAHEAL flag for mana rooms.
{G}FIRETRAP                      Fire comes up from the ground and burns members in the room. 
                              Dex+Int is used in avoidance. Damage ranges from 1 to 30 hp.
{B}ROCKTRAP                      Rocks fall from the ceiling. Based on Dex and Int. Damage ranges 
                              from 1 to 50 hp.
{G}ARROWTRAP                     Arrows shoot out and hit characters in the room. Dex, wis,
                              and Int allow avoidance. Damages from 1 to 25, but good 
                              magic armor or natural armor helps in absorbing this damage.
{B}POISONTRAP                    Same as arrow trap except the arrows are poison-tipped.
{G}SPIKETRAP                     people fall onto spikes. 1 to 35 damage, but depends on 
                              natural/magic armor.
{B}GASTRAP2                      1 to 35 damage; gas chokes the character, and may poison. 
                              No saving from stats. Dont use gastrap1 it doesnt work!!
{G}AVALANCHE                     This room trap only goes off once! (total!!!, not even each 
                              reboot!). it does 10-55 damage regardless, and 20-40 more
                              33% of the time (trapped under the snow).
{B}GYSERTRAP                     Scalding water hits the character. 10-40 damage.
{G}MANADRAIN                     Slow or negative mana regen in this room. Reported to be 
                              problematic, although not proven. (infinite mana?) 
                              On my mud it does give infinite mana nice work 
                              Owen Emlen(tm) code :)
{B}IS_VEHICLE {R}Dont use{B}                   See section on the next page on vehicle rooms.
{G}CLANSTORE                     Marks this room as a clan storage location. This MUST 
                              be within 20 vnums of the clans starting vnum, as 
                              specified in CEDIT (clan editor) See later section
                              on Cedit.
{B}ACIDSPRAY                     Not Implemented.

 
{W}See Also: PET-SHOPS, RSTAT, ROOM-FLAGS, RESETS, RESET1, RESET2, COUNT, SECTOR
{g}
~

101 'IREF OEDIT' OEDIT~
OEDIT <vnum> or OEDIT create <vnum> enters the OBJECT editor.

The following commands are available from within the OEDITOR:

show                - hitting return, or 'show' shows the object stats
done                - exits the object editor and returns to normal play
timer <# of ticks>  - sets the timed age of an object (automated self-destruct)
name <keywords>     - sets the keywords on an object
short <desc>        - sets the 'name' of an object (a sword, a fish etc)
long                - edit long description (the one in the room)
value0 <num>        - sets the value '0' on the object (also abbrev.d to 'v0')
value1 <num>        - sets the value '1' on the object (also abbrev.d to 'v1')
value2 <num>        - sets the value '2' on the object (also abbrev.d to 'v2')
value3 <num>        - sets the value '3' on the object (also abbrev.d to 'v3')
weight <stones>     - sets the weight of the object
cost <gold>         - sets the gold value of the object
create <vnum>       - creates object with specified vnum
ed add <keyword>    - type this for adding/editing extended descriptions
addaffect           - type this for info on adding object affects/applies
remaffect           - removes an affect on an object
You may also type the name of the object type (see IREF OBJ-TYPES) or
you can type the name of the extra bit you want to toggle (IREF EXTRA-FLAGS).
You can also type the name of an affect (see AFFECT-BITS), but do __NOT__
use these without asking a god first.

See Also: OSTAT, WEAR-LOCATIONS, OBJ-VALUES, WEAPONS, OBJ-VALFLAGS, LIQUIDS,
          CLIMBABLE, ADDAFFECTS, STANDARD, LOCATIONS, RESETS,
          RESET2, FURNITURE, CREATING, (I-COLORS) >To set colors to objects
~

101 'IREF MEDIT' MEDIT~
MEDIT alone enters the MOBILE editor.

The following commands are available from within the MEDITOR:

show                - hitting return, or 'show' shows the mobile stats
done                - exits the mobile editor and returns to normal play
timer <# of ticks>  - sets the timed age of an mobile (automated self-destruct)
name <keywords>     - sets the keywords on an mobile
short <desc>        - sets the 'name' of an mobile (a sword, a fish etc)
long                - edit long description (the one in the room)
desc                - edit the mobile's description (when looked at)
shop                - type this command for further information
create <vnum>       - creates mobile with specified vnum
male/female/neuter  - set the mobile's sex
level <level>       - set the mobile's level
alignment <value>   - set the mobile's alignment
attack <num> <type> <min dam> <max dam>
                    - number 1-5, type (see IREF WEAPONS), min/max dam
                      these are extra attacks for mobiles, use intelligently
money <amount>      - set the amount of gold loaded on a mob (use sparingly)
alter <vnum>        - At 10pm and 5 am, the mob transforms into vnum mob.
guarding <vnum/dir> - Set this mob to guard a direction, item, or mob.
                      They can only guard one of these, so don't set their
                      act3 bits to anymore than one guard task.

You may also type the name of the act bits to toggle (see IREF ACT-BITS), or
you can type the name of the affect you want the mob to have (see the help on
IREF AFFECT-BITS) AND you can also type the name of the spec function you
want (see IREF SPEC-PROCS).

See Also: GUARDING MOBS, MSTAT, MFIND, MSET, PET-SHOPS, LOCATIONS, MOB-TYPES, STANDARD, 
          HP, RESETS, RESET1, SWITCH, FORCE, SCRIPTS, SHOPS, BUILDING, CREATING
~

103 'guarding mobs'~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                               {R}GUARDING MOBS
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}

Guarding mobs
-------------

3guard_door          - Sets the mob to guard a direction from all intruders.
3guard_door_evil     - Guards a specified direction from evil characters.
3guard_door_good     - Guards a specified direction from good characters.
clan <number>        - Only admins have to worry about this command.
                       If set, the mob will guard in the direction specified
                       and will only allow the clan members through.
Guarding <direction> - This will set the direction the mob will guard.
3guard_item          - Sets the mob to guard an item specified in guarding <vnum>
3guard_mob           - Sets the mob to guard another mob specified by guarding <vnum>
guarding <vnum> Specifies the item vnum or mob vnum to guard MUST BE LESS THEN 32000
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N} 
~

103 'IMMORTAL COMMANDS'~
The following is a very incomplete list...

               -* Implementor Commands *-
advance   - advance player levels
trust     - trust players to higher level
                -* Demi-god Commands *-
aedit     - enter area editor
shutdown  - shut down mud
allow     - remove a banned site from the ban list
ban       - ban a site
deny      - deny a player
mset      - set stats on a mob
oset      - set stats on an object
sset      - set skills on a player
log       - log a player's actions
memory    - get memory information
                 -* Supreme Commands *-
pset      - set a players stats
discon    - disconnect a player
freeze    - freeze a player
reboot    - reboot the mud
wizlock   - lock the mud for immortal/wizified logins only
force     - force a player to do a command
noemote   - take away a player's emote privilege
notell    - take away a player's tell privilege
silence   - take away a player's ability to talk at all
slay      - kill a player w/o combat
at        - temporary version of 'goto'
echo      - echo a message to the entire mud
switch    - switch into a mob
return    - return from being switched
snoop     - snoop a player's session
                     -* Angel Commands *-
pardon    - take away thief/killer flag
unpardon  - place thief/killer flag
peace     - stop all combat in the room
recho     - echo to just the room
                    -* Builder Commands *-
redit     - enter room editor
oedit     - enter object editor
medit     - enter mobile editor
mindex    - look at a mob's index
oindex    - look at an object's index
oload     - load an object
mload     - load a mob
mstat     - stat a mobile
astat     - stat an area
pstat     - stat a player
asave     - save the zone/database/list
mfind     - find a mob in the database
ofind     - find an object in the database
ostat     - stat an object
rstat     - stat the room your in
slookup   - look up the skillnumber of a particular slot
purge     - clear all mobs/objs in the room other than players
script    - show the script of a mobile (if any)
             -* Immortal Commands *-
users     - show users and sites currently logged on
restore   - restore the stats of a user
transfer  - teleport a player/monster
wizify    - set a wiz bit so players can log in during wizlock
bamfin    - set the message players see when you appear using 'goto'
bamfout   - set the message players see when you disappear using 'goto'
goto      - transfer yourself to a player/room/mobile/object
holylight - see in the dark/invis/magic auras etc
invis     - turn wizinvis on so players / lower level immorts cant see you
mwhere    - find a mob in the mud
owhere    - find an object in the mud
notify    - useful command (type 'notify help')
              -* Hero Commands *-
immtalk   - talk to immort channel
]         - same as above
autostat  - show room stats when moving around

~

0 SKAVEN~
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
                                    {R}Skaven
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
{N}Skavens have a past of being filthy, slum dwelling humanoids.  Most of
the skaven ancestors have been thiefs or shamans, but the occasional
warrior can be found among the mass quanities of these rat-like humans.
Skavens are the mutation of a rat to gain the strength and intellect of a
human.  Skaven can be only evil, for they hate human kind.

{d}Inherant Abilities: 

{G}Immune to poison, Infravision, and Detect Hidden.

{N}Skaven {C}gain {N}a {g}small {N}bonuses to Strength and Contitution.
{N}Skaven {C}gain {N}a {G}large {N}bonuses to Dexterity.
{N}Skaven {R}suffer {N}a {G}large {N}penalty to Intelligence and Wisdom.

Help file created by: {R}Kilith{N}
{d}[{R}+{d}]{B}-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-{d}[{R}+{d}]{N}
~

{N}Wild elves, in general, are those elves who have recluded from society and
are living hardened lives outside of the elven community.  Wild elves can
be considered a different race due to their small difference in anatomy.
Wild elves' skin is covered in a set of stripes that are a variety in color,
texture and size.  In addition to the multicolored stripes, wild elves
have a keen sense of their surroundings.  Like elves, Wild elves also can see
in the dark using their natural ability for infravision.

{N}The exact origins of the thri-kreen have been lost in the mists of time,
however myth says they once lived in great hives in the tropical forests.
However their kind has not been seen upon the surface of the world in any great
numbers in centuries. Rumor has it that they Thri-Kreen moved beneath the
surface to escape the approach of mankind, however there may be other reasons.

Half man and half insect, the thri-kreen do not readily adapt to the society of
human folk. As a natural self defense mechanism, the Thri-kreen coat their
weapons with a poisonous venom which their bodies produce. Thri-kreen appear
to have a natural tolerance to poison and disease, a attribute of their
insectoid ancestry.

Inherant Abilities:
